< text>
I will miss you Pauline‚Äôs.  I ate here my first night in my long time apartment about 500ft away from you, almost 10 years ago to this day. I had been in then city for less than a month, and was scrambling to find a place and after much battling finally found one right near Pauline‚Äôs. In fact, when I looked at the apartment, the lady said, it‚Äôs not much but you are steps away from the best pizza in the city. So, our first night here we checked it out. I had gotten way over dressed to eat at your restaurant, but after the stress of moving and other stress looming, we both though it would be fun to look our finest. We were shocked when we got there, and there was a bundle of crayons, with a table cloth to draw on. A good fun. Both of our eyes light up, as we‚Äôd unleash our inner artists on the table. As My then-fianc√©, (now husband) and I drew on the table with crayons, and fell in love with your amazing pesto pizza, and sundaes, and salads that were nostalgia encapsulated for me, they reminded me of the ones my mom made from the vegetables my dad grew in the garden. The salads here, always a bit different, still always tasted like childhood, like summer too me. We were broke, our first time eating here, after just paying security, first and last months rent, but we splurged had a glass of your wine. We were happy to be here but also struck with a bit of fear, as I had just learned I had cancer, less than 24 hours after making the cross country move here. But we forgot about all that for a moment and we talked and we laughed about our dreams of our new life inSan Francisco, and how excited we were to have a special like this so close to us. We‚Äôve come many times over the years, picked up many pesto pizzas to eat home together on the bed. Sometimes, I‚Äôd get a craving for just one of the crunchy breadstick it came with. This, our block has changed so much, up and down over the last decade. Some for the better, some for the worse. But losing Pauline‚Äôs, has been the biggest loss. This restaurant to me was one that captured the soul, I so love of San Francisco. And still fight for, because it‚Äôs the piece that I still love, but that light is flickering, even more now. Losing one beloved place, one special only in San Francisco place after another. (It makes me so sad, no one wanted to buy Pauline‚Äôs and keep its beautiful legacy going). At least I will always have the memories of this place in my heart, and I‚Äôm sure I‚Äôm the hearts of many others that looked on this place with emense fondness. <Review>If you're looking for a classic NY or Chicago Pie, you've come to the wrong place. If you're looking for fresh and unique California pies, come on in!

I agree with the other reviews: the pesto pie is not to be missed. It's basic - just salty pesto and pine nuts on a crust, but it's super flavorful. No cheese, no toppings. It would be nice with some rounds of melted fresh mozz, grilled chicken, maybe diced tomato, but it's great how it is, too. The special pizzas of the day are a good way to go. One of my favorites was topped with butternut squash. Unexpected and delicious! For meat pies, the best so far was one with salami or something on it. I'm mostly a fan of the veggie pies, though. Thanks to their garden, the toppings on the veggie pizzas are always fresh and high qual. Ooooh, and don't forget the wine. Makes for a great buzz to go with your pies!

Good for groups and parties. Call ahead - reservations come in handy.<//Review><Name>Veronica Lujan</Name><UserId.>113809335863491226852< /UserId.>< time>

Much of what is appealing on the menu is not available for pickup (ie: any of the build-your-own pancakes) and they deny the existance of the kids meals mentioned on their online menu.  Several things were wrong with my order.  They had to remake one set of pancakes entirely (check EVERY box before you leave) and even then I pointed out several things that were missed.

I would think 7 months into a global pandemic, "take-out" would be second nature... but it seemed like this was the first "to-go" order this establishment has ever done.

< Review>
Claim Jumper is a great spot to go for Happy Hour or a meal before an event or game at Golden 1 Center. The Happy Hour menu is extensive, but all the food and beverages are fairly priced for the quantity and quality of food they provide. While the location to the arena is a block or so further away than other options, Claim Jumper is much less crowded, with friendly staff in an elegant venue. This place is a favorite of locals and Sacramento Kings fans!<//Review>

Living in Midtown, I have so many great dining options, mostly non-chain/franchise. But I tried Claim Jumper for a Happy Hour dinner and liked it enough to leave a review. Definitely some excellent food values and I got to sample the tacos and potato skins for bargain prices, along with a nice draft beer.

Good options for making a dinner from the Happy Hour menu. Maybe next time I'll try the full menu, which is pricier.

This is a gorgeous place, as it used to be the upscale seafood restaurant McCormick & Schmicks, and has lots of elegant wood and nice aesthetics overall.< /Text>

< Text>
This might have been one of the worst dining experiences of my life. It's been several years since I've been to a claim jumper and boy has the restaurant changed. The portions are smaller now, which probably is a good thing, but the prices are still very high. So it's as if they've reduced the portion sizes and kept the old prices.

That wasn't even the worst part. When we arrived our table was dirty, and it was no silverware. There was a delay in our starters and appetizers, and all of our food came out at the same time. My wife had ordered a salad bar, which seemed unattended. No one was using the salad bar, and there was a reason for that.

Our food arrived, like I said at the same time. And the food was average at best. I had the blackened salmon which was okay, I had asked for roasted vegetables, but I received sauteed vegetables. My wife's pasta was soaked in oil and was gross. How hard is it to get a seafood pasta dish right?

Anyhow, after our food arrived, we still did not have silverware or napkins despite asking twice for them from two different servers. As we looked around, we noticed other tables had the same dilemma. As we noticed each other everyone started laughing about how sad it was. The guy next to me had a steak and just had to stare at it for 5 minutes. Eventually I got up after losing my patience at which point the staff jump to attention.

I don't know what happened to claim jumper. It used to be such a fun place to go with my family. But now it's a disgrace. I was embarrassed for myself and for my family. I apologized and told them we would never be back. And I will not be back with anyone else.< /Text>

<Text>I came here on August 17th at 7:00 pm to celebrate my birthday with 15 of my friends. I reserved weeks in advance due to us being a larger party. I have gone to the Claimjumper's in Roseville for my last 4 birthday's and received stellar service each time... So I expected similar from this location. This is not what myself or those in my party experienced.

1. It was announced without prompt that we would be automatically charged a tip of 22% as our menus were being passed out. Which in my opinion was rude.

2. We were expected to not change seats. As host of my group I needed to sit with everyone and provide my time to them. We were catching up and enjoying eachother's time. But we were told we ought to remain in our seats and keep the seat we started in.

3. It was extraordinarily hot in the restaurant. I was literally sweating and feeling faint. The pregnant woman in my party had to leave to get air as she was feeling faint as well. All of us were uncomfortably hot. We reported this issue twice. Each time we were told there was nothing they could do due to this being an "old" building. Okay, so it's okay for patrons to feel faint? What would staff had done if one of us had actually passed out? That sure sounds like a lawsuit waiting to happen.

4. One guest was never provided a drink. No refills on drinks were offered at any point. We normally spend $300-400 on drinks alone each year we come. Claimjumper's lost this revenue as no one came by to provide refills or take requests.

5. Condiments were missing and orders were wrong or missing. I don't believe anyone checked on us once we were served. These mistakes were not remedied. Though one person received their appetizer after they finished dinner. Butter was also not served with the bread. We asked. Nothing came.

6. The pregnant woman in my party was provided a cup with mold in it. She did not see it until her water was almost finished.

7. My birthday cake came without the traditional song from staff. The cake was hard and came 30 minutes after finishing our meals. It was not the layered chocolate cake as advertised in the flyer sitting in front of me.

8. My sister could not locate a manager and she had to complain to another member of the service staff. We had no idea where our server was at.

9. We were done with our meal for 40-50 minutes before our checks arrived. Oh.. They're coming we hear... When they did finally come the checks came incorrect or were incomplete, we actually had to request our checks be provided. I could not locate my check and no one responded to my request to locate it and I finally gave up. Technically, I got a free meal due to staff's lack of attention. Again, more lost revenue. Nor does an accidental free meal make up for this night's shotty service.

10. Our server reappeared after my sister's complaint. She offered a free drink as compensation. Where was she when we wanted refills and were ready to spend lavishly on drinks? By now it was a little too late. By then we were so annoyed and fatigued from the heat we just wanted to be done and go.

11. This ruined my birthday. No one including myself had the energy to continue with the night's plans. We were hot and sweating, and truly unhappy with this restaurant's service. We called it a night from there when we had plans that would take us late into the night.

I have never received more dismal service from a Claimjumper's restaurant than I did here. We were there to spend a lot of money and have a good time, neither of which we could do. Some of us are getting together again to have a "redo" party which is asinine to say the least, but my friends felt so bad for me it's the least they felt they could do.< /Text><pics>None</pics>< response>

< review>
Specifically the downtown, Sacramento location: I first ate here the year they opened downtown, after Mccormick & Schmick‚Äôs (I liked that place) and I had a pretty lackluster experience; the food was subpar and the service was incredibly lacking. Years go by, and I started craving their Motherlode cake.  So, after a ridiculously great dinner at Cattlemen's, I talk up the cake to my dinner party. I drive to the downtown. Claim Jumper and order ONE slice of the Motherlode cake. I'm tired, full, and ready to go home, so I tell the hostess an order to go, please. It's not busy so the wait shouldn't be long. She tells me 10 to 15 minutes. I should mention it's Saturday and I'm parked in their passenger loading area with a car full of people. I ask why so long and she just says 10 minutes, max. Then I ask, but why, aren't you just dropping it in a box? She just says 10 minutes, like a broken, perpetually skipping record. I may sound a little high strung, but that just seems stupid to me. Personally, I'm surprised this location still exists. I'm going to truck to Roseville tomorrow for this cake. I'm swearing off this downtown location, I've had enough bad service for this year.<//review>
